IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO(S).             OF 2026
(@ SPECIAL LEAVE PETITION (CRL.) NO.(S)11501 OF 2024)
MUKESH SHARMA                              APPELLANT
                                VERSUS
VINOD KUMAR AGRAWAL                        RESPONDENT
WITH
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO(S).               OF 2026
(@SPECIAL LEAVE PETITION (CRL.) NO.(S)11702 OF 2024)
O R D E R
Leave granted.
2. Present  Appeals  have  been  filed
challenging the order dated 06 th March 2024
passed by the High Court of Judicature for
Rajasthan at Jodhpur, whereby the complaints
under  Section  138  of  the  Negotiable
Instruments Act, 1881 (for short, “NI Act”)
instituted by the appellant were transferred
from Bhilwara to Ajmer on the ground that a
charge  sheet  has  been  filed  against  the
appellant in Ajmer for the offences under
Sections 403 and 417 of the IPC in relation
to the subject-matter of cheques in question.
1

--- Page 14 ---
3. A perusal of the paper book reveals that
vide  order  dated  20 th August  2024,  the
predecessor  Bench  had  issued  notice  and
stayed the impugned order passed by the High
Court. The paper book further reveals that
despite completion of service, no one has
appeared or filed Vakalatnama on behalf of
the respondent. Consequently, this Court has
no option but to proceed with the hearing of
the present appeals. 
4. Learned  counsel  for  the  appellant
submits that it is settled law that the Court
within whose jurisdiction the branch of the
bank where the payee maintains the account is
situated, will have jurisdiction to try the
offence  if  the  cheque  is  delivered  for
collection through an account. He states that
the cause of action in the present case arose
in Bhilwara since appellant maintains his
bank  account  in  Kotak  Mahindra  Bank,
Bhilwara. He further points out that though
trial  had  commenced  in  the  appellant’s
complaint way  back in  2019, the  Transfer
Petitions had been filed in the year 2022. 
2

--- Page 15 ---
5. This Court finds that a coordinate Bench
in Jai Balaji Industries Ltd. v. M/s HEG Ltd.
2025 SCC OnLine SC 2581  has held that the
jurisdiction to try a complaint filed under
Section 138 of the NI Act in respect of a
cheque delivered for connection through an
account, i.e., an account payee cheque, is
vested  in  the  Court  within  whose  local
jurisdiction the branch of the bank in which
the payee maintains the account. This Court
also finds that evidence has commenced in the
complaint  filed  by  the  appellant  under
Section 138 of the NI Act way back in 2019.
Consequently, the jurisdiction vests in the
Court  where  the  payee's  home  branch,  is
situated.
6. Accordingly, this Court is of the view
that  the  Courts  in  Bhilwara  have  the
exclusive jurisdiction to enquire into and
try the offences under Section 138 of NI Act
alleged  to  have  been  committed  by  the
appellant. 
7. Therefore,  the  present  appeals  are
allowed and the order dated 06 th March 2024
3

--- Page 16 ---
passed by the High Court of Judicature for
Rajasthan at Jodhpur is set aside.
………………………………………………………, J
    (MANMOHAN)
…………………………………………………………, J
       (K. VINOD CHANDRAN)
NEW DELHI;
JULY 01, 2026
4

UPON hearing the counsel the Court made 
the following
           O R D E R
I.A. NO. 180474/2026 IN CRIMINAL APPEAL 
NO. 3031/2026
The  appellant/applicant  has  been
convicted for the offence punishable under
Section 120-B of the Indian Penal Code,
1860.
Learned Senior Counsel appearing for
the applicant submits that the applicant
has been on bail for past 20 years. He
2

--- Page 25 ---
further  submits  that  the  applicant  has
been under custody for more than 5 years
and 8 months.
Learned Senior Counsel appearing for
the  respondent  vehemently  opposed  the
application inter-alia contending that the
reasons assigned by the High Court could
not warrant suspension of sentence.
Leave has been granted and the appeal
is pending on the file of this Court. We
find that both the issues of fact and law
ought to be decided in the appeal. It is
not in dispute that for nearly 20 years
the applicant has been enlarged on bail.
Considering  the  above  alongwith  the
period of incarceration undergone, we are
inclined to suspend the sentence of the
applicant and grant bail to him, during
3

--- Page 26 ---
the pendency of this appeal
Accordingly, the sentence imposed upon
the applicant stands suspended and he is
granted bail, subject to the terms and
conditions  that  may  be  imposed  by  the
trial court, during the pendency of the
appeal.
IA  No.  180474/2026  is,  accordingly,
allowed.
(PRIYANKA MALIK)         (POONAM VAID)
COURT MASTER (SH)      ASSISTANT REGISTRAR

sentence, during the pendency of the present appeal.
The appellant has been convicted for the offences
punishable under Section 3(3) of t he Terrorist and
Disruptive Activities (Prevention) Act, 1987 (for
short, the TADA  Act) read with Section 120B of the
Indian Penal Code, and he was sentenced to undergo
rigorous imprisonment for a period of five years
along with fine. 
Admittedly,  out  of  the  sentence  of  five
years  which  has  been  awarded,  the
applicant/appellant  has  already  undergone
incarceration for a period of three years and nine
months.  The  appeal  is  also  likely  to  take
substantial time for its disposal.
Considering the above circumstances, we are
inclined to suspend the sentence awarded to the
applicant/appellant and grant bail to him, during
the pendency of the present appeal.
Accordingly, the sentence imposed upon the
applicant/appellant  stands  suspended,  and  he  is
granted regular bail, during the pendency of the
appeal, subject to the terms and conditions that may
be imposed by the concerned Trial Court
The applications are allowed, accordingly.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CRIMINAL APPEAL No.2371/2024
PALLAVI SRIVASTAVA & ANR.                          APPELLANTS
                                VERSUS
STATE OF U.P. & ORS.                              RESPONDENTS
 O R D E R
1.  The appellants were before the High Court under Section
482 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, 1973 (for short, the
Cr.PC) to quash FIR No.133 dated 09.04.2023 registered at
Police Station Rasra, District Ballia, Uttar Pradesh under
Sections 504 and 507 of the Indian Penal Code, 1860 (for
short, the IPC).
2. The primary contention raised is that an investigation
cannot be carried out as against the offences alleged
without an order of the Magistrate since both are non-
cognizable offences. 
3. The impugned order has just quoted two judgments of this
Court regarding arrest of accused, as provided under the
Cr.PC and merely disposed of the case, opining that the
guidelines framed by this Court would be applicable to the
facts of the instant case. 
4. We  were  inclined  to  remand  the  matter  for  fresh
consideration but the learned counsel for the respondent
State, on instructions, submits that now a final report has
been filed before the learned Magistrate. 

--- Page 38 ---
5. The learned counsel for the appellants pointed out that the
learned Magistrate could still take cognizance, even if the
final report finds no evidence to proceed with the trial.  
6. These  are  contentions  which  could  be  urged  by  the
appellants before the jurisdictional Court when the final
report is taken up for consideration; when, the question of
the investigation carried out without an order of the
Magistrate, as provided under Section 155 (2) of the Cr.PC,
as against non-cognizable offences can also be urged.
7. With the above observations, the Criminal Appeal stands
disposed  of  as  infructuous  along  with  all  pending
applications.
…………………………………………………J.
                                        (MANMOHAN)          
 
  …………………………………………………J.
                                        (K. VINOD CHANDRAN) 
NEW DELHI; 
JULY 02, 2026

None is present for the appellant.
2. Even on the last two dates of hearing, none was present
for the appellant. Consequently, this Court has no other option
but to proceed with the matter.
3. A perusal of the paper book it reveals that limited
notice was issued by this Court on 19.10.2009 confined to the
question as to whether the appellant is entitled to subsistence
allowance from 04.04.1997 to 27.09.2001. 
4. In the counter Affidavit filed by the High Court of
Himachal Pradesh, it has been stated as under:
“15. The Respondent was always ready and willing and
is ready and willing to pay the subsistence allowance
to the petitioner for the period in question as per
office order dated 08.02.2002, but in absence of the
requisite certificate, it was not possible for the
District Judge, Hamirpur, as well as the High Court to
prepare necessary bills and submit the same to the
treasury. The treasury would not sanction the payment,
until the requisite certificate are appended.
16. The petitioner in this SLP has filed certain
certificates at pages 103 and 104 of the paper book,
but the said certificate are not available in the
office of the District Judge, Hamirpur or the Himachal
Pradesh High Court. If the petitioner submits the
necessary certificates, as required under FR 53(2) and
prescribed under CCA (CCS) Rules, 1965, the payment
would be processed forthwith.”

aforesaid paragraphs of the counter affidavit.

Pradesh in paragraphs 15 and 16 of the counter affidavit is
accepted by this Court.
7. Holding  respondent  No.1  bound  by  the  aforesaid

ITEM NO.1               COURT NO.6               SECTION II-C
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Petition(s) for Special Leave to Appeal (Crl.)  No(s).  11227/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  02-03-2026
in CRMPM No. 128/2026 passed by the High Court of Himachal Pradesh
at Shimla]
ARVINDER SINGH @ BILLA                             Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
STATE OF HIMACHAL PRADESH                          Respondent(s)
(IA No. 178246/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING C/C OF THE IMPUGNED 
JUDGMENT
IA No. 178248/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.)
 
Date : 02-07-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE MANMOHAN 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE K. VINOD CHANDRAN
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) : Mr. Siddharth Jain, AOR
                   
For Respondent(s)  Mr. Kartikeya Rastogi, D.A.G.
                   Ms. Inderdeep Kaur Raina, Adv.
                   Ms. Tamanna Kavdia, Adv.
                   Mr. Rohit Bansal, AOR
                   
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. The  present  Special  Leave  Petition  has  been  filed
challenging the order dated 02.03.2026 passed by the Himachal
Pradesh High Court dismissing the regular Bail Application of
the petitioner-accused, who has been charged with possession of
29.84 grams of Heroin under Narcotic Drugs and Psychotropic
Substances Act (for short “NDPS Act”). 
2. Keeping in view the five criminal antecedents of the
petitioner, this Court is of the view that he is not entitled
1

--- Page 44 ---
to bail on merits.
3. At this stage, learned counsel for the petitioner presses
I.A. No.180806/2026, praying for admission in a Government
Recognised  De-addiction/  Rehabilitation  Centre  so  that
Petitioner  can  undergo  treatment,  counselling  and
rehabilitation in accordance with law.
4. The said prayer(s) has been opposed by the Respondent-
State by filing a reply on the ground that the benefit of
Section 64A of the NDPS Act is not intended to give protection
to persons involved in illegal possession or trafficking of
Narcotics  substances  like  Chitta/Heroin.  According  to  the
Respondent-State, the benefit of Section 64A can be availed
only by a consumer of narcotics charged under Section 27 of the
NDPS  Act  or  with  offences  involving  possession  of  small
quantity of narcotic drugs.
5. This Court finds that in the present case the Petitioner
is charged not under Section 27 of NDPS Act, but under Section
21 of the NDPS Act and that too for possession of intermediate
quantity of narcotic substances. In any event, this Court find
that there is no medical record from jail authority (despite
the Petitioner having been in custody for more than ten months)
to  show  that  the  Petitioner  is  a  drug  addict  requiring
rehabilitation  or  that  he  is  suffering  from  withdrawal
symptoms.
2

--- Page 45 ---
6. Accordingly,  the  present  Special  Leave  Petition  is
dismissed along with all pending applications.
(RADHA SHARMA)                                  (DIVYA BABBAR)
ASTT. REGISTRAR-cum-PS                        COURT MASTER (NSH)
3

--- Page 46 ---

IA No. 148191/2025 - GRANT OF BAIL
The applicant-appellant has been charged

--- Page 113 ---
2
and convicted for the offence punishable under
Section 302 of the Indian Penal Code, 1860.
 While  the  Trial  Court  acquitted  the
appellant,  the  High  Court  was  pleased  to
reverse  it  and  sentence  him  to  undergo
imprisonment for life.
Taking  note  of  the  conflicting  views
taken by both the Courts, and the period of
incarceration  undergone  by  him,  we  are
inclined  to  suspend  the  sentence  of  the
appellant, during the pendency of his appeal.
Accordingly,  the  sentence  of  the
appellant is suspended and he is granted bail,
during the pendency of the appeal, on terms
and conditions to the satisfaction of the
Trial Court.
List the appeal in the second week of
February, 2027.

                             O R D E R
Heard  the  learned  Senior  Counsel  appearing  for  the
petitioners.
Delay condoned.
Learned Senior Counsel appearing for the petitioners raises
two grounds: one is with respect to the petitioners share and the
other is on the entitlement to the property as per the will.
In so far as the entitlement to the property, as per the will
is  concerned,  the  law  is  quite  settled  that  any  number  of
preliminary decrees can be passed, and therefore, there is no bar
for the petitioners to seek another preliminary decree.
1

--- Page 129 ---
In so far as the contention on the shares being wrongly
allotted, liberty is given to the petitioners to file a review
petition before the High Court, within a period of four weeks from
the date of receipt of a copy of this order.
In the event of the review petition being dismissed, the
petitioners can challenge the present impugned judgment on that
score alone.
Accordingly, the special leave petition is disposed of.
Pending application(s), if any, shall also stand disposed of.

Mr.Tushar Mehta, learned Solicitor General for India, who is
present in Court.

that identical issues are pending in W.P.(C)No.708/2026.

--- Page 165 ---
2
6. Let  the  present  writ  petition  be  tagged  with  W.P.
(C)No.708/2026.
7. At this stage Mr. Jayant Singh Raghav, petitioner no.3
submits that on 05.07.2026 Haryana Public Service Commission is
conducting examination for recruitment for Assistant District
Attorney in Prosecution Department, Haryana. The petitioner
nos.2 and 3 (visually disabled) apprehend that on 05.07.2026
they will not be given the benefit of a scribe to write the
said examination.
8. Without prejudice to the rights and contentions of the
parties,  we  direct  the  Chairman,  Haryana  Public  Service
Commission to personally look into the matter and provide a
scribe to write the said examination for Ms. Sara Chawla -
petitioner no.2 and Mr. Jayant Singh Raghav - petitioner no.3,
who are visually disabled and who under the Scribe guidelines
dated  20.08.2018  are  entitled  for  scribes  to  write  the
examination.
